vervecoach — FULL ORCHESTRATOR TRANSCRIPT
==========================================

ORIGINAL PROMPT
---------------
PORTFOLIO_CHILD_PROJECT: true
Parent portfolio: multi-app-exp4
Selected app slug: vervecoach

Build this app as a working local-first SwiftUI MVP.

## Selected App Spec

# VerveCoach

Build mode: **MVP build**.
Build priority: **6**.

## App Name

VerveCoach

## Category

professional-communication

## One-Sentence Promise

Rehearse the conversations that matter before you walk into the room.

## Target User

Managers, founders, interview candidates, salespeople, and professionals who need to prepare for emotionally or financially important conversations.

## Painful Moment Solved

The user has one difficult conversation coming up and knows improvising will go badly.

## Why It Is Different

Rehearsal-driven, not a generic chat assistant or note pad; the product is about practicing responses under pressure.

## Why Users Would Pay

Better communication changes outcomes in interviews, negotiations, feedback conversations, and sales calls.

## Subscription Model

Free limited rehearsal scenarios; premium for unlimited sessions, custom scenario libraries, progress history, advanced coaching modes.

## Local-First MVP Scope

Scenario setup, role-based prompt cards, rehearsal flows, reflection notes, session history, optional on-device critique where available.

## Future Backend Roadmap

Cross-device sync, shared coaching templates, mentor review, richer speech analysis.

## AR / Local ML / Local LLM Fit

An on-device LLM is useful for critique and response variation, but the app ships strong rule-based rehearsal flows and fallbacks.

## Design Direction

Confident, minimal, psychologically safe with low-friction rehearsal cards and strong focus states.

## App Store Positioning

A private rehearsal app for people who need better outcomes from the conversations that matter.

## Invalidation Criteria

If the app is just a prompt box asking an AI what to say, it fails.

## v1 Build Scope

Local scenario rehearsal app with manual setup, guided response practice, audio capture, review notes, optional model-backed critique where supported, onboarding, paywall, persistence.

## Core Workflows

- Define a real upcoming conversation
- Rehearse likely turns and responses
- Review weak spots and next-best phrasing

## iOS-Native Features

- Speech recognition
- Audio recording
- App Intents for quick rehearsal starts
- Widgets for upcoming sessions
- Local notifications

## Key Risks

- LLM dependency must not become a device-eligibility trap
- Could drift into generic self-help if rehearsal structure is weak

## Claude Design Handoff Prompt

Design an iPhone rehearsal app for difficult conversations with calm focus, strong voice interaction, scenario setup, and premium coaching feedback surfaces.

## Parent Portfolio Prompt

Build 7 completely separate iOS apps at the same time.

Requirements:
1. Each app must go from 0 to production-ready, not just a few features.
2. Each app must be unique, useful, and commercially viable.
3. Each app must be beautifully designed and feel premium.
4. Each app must provide real end-user value.
5. Each app should have a realistic path to monetization, with a subscription or paid offering that offers genuine value.
6. Each app should have viral potential in general or within a niche, but virality must not come at the expense of usefulness.
7. Each app should be better than its competitors in a meaningful way.
8. Each app should be local-first, but architected so cloud support could be added later without rewriting everything.
9. The seven apps must not be similar to each other.
10. No app can be similar to anything I have already built before — including the apps already in this workspace (e.g. Waylay and TrueScale, currently in progress).
11. Do not reuse prior concepts, themes, or mechanics from earlier apps unless there is a strong, clearly justified reason.

Bonus points:
- Unique use of LLMs
- Unique use of AR
- Unique use of ML

Important:
- Bonus points are optional. Do not force them in if they would weaken the app.
- If an LLM, AR, or ML feature is used, it must provide real value and be integral to the product.
- Do not bias the ideas toward bonus points.
- Do not make the app around novelty alone.
- The final result for each app must be a full production-ready app, not a prototype.

Build rules:
- Run the seven app efforts in parallel.
- Keep the discussion and design phases separate for each app.
- Each app should get its own full product direction, design direction, architecture, implementation plan, and build output.
- Save all prompt discussion, phase discussion, and final decisions for each app.
- At the end, combine the full transcript for each app into a .txt file.
- If an app is liked, also prepare a Jira board and Notion project for it separately, including epics, tasks, fields, and all the implementation structure needed for backfilling later.
- If the system supports multiple rounds per phase, use enough rounds to get high-quality discussion, but allow a phase to end early if consensus is reached.
- Make the orchestrator resilient: if a phase stalls, recover cleanly instead of looping.
- Report only important milestones, not every tiny step.

Output:
- Create one folder per app in the output directory.
- There must be one folder per app, not one folder containing all apps.
- Keep the outputs clearly separated and organized.

Output directory:
- /Users/pchordia/Documents/iOS-App-Factory

Now generate candidate app ideas (at least 10), discuss them thoroughly, choose the best 7, and build all seven to production quality.

```
# VerveCoach

## App Name

VerveCoach

## Category

professional-communication

## One-Sentence Promise

Rehearse the conversations that matter before you walk into the room.

## Target User

Managers, founders, interview candidates, salespeople, and professionals who need to prepare for emotionally or financially important conversations.

## Painful Moment Solved

The user has one difficult conversation coming up and knows improvising will go badly.

## Why It Is Different

Rehearsal-driven, not a generic chat assistant or note pad; the product is about practicing responses under pressure.

## Why Users Would Pay

Better communication changes outcomes in interviews, negotiations, feedback conversations, and sales calls.

## Subscription Model

Free limited rehearsal scenarios; premium for unlimited sessions, custom scenario libraries, progress history, advanced coaching modes.

## Local-First MVP Scope

Scenario setup, role-based prompt cards, rehearsal flows, reflection notes, session history, optional on-device critique where available.

## Future Backend Roadmap

Cross-device sync, shared coaching templates, mentor review, richer speech analysis.

## AR / Local ML / Local LLM Fit

An on-device LLM is useful for critique and response variation, but the app ships strong rule-based rehearsal flows and fallbacks.

## Design Direction

Confident, minimal, psychologically safe with low-friction rehearsal cards and strong focus states.

## App Store Positioning

A private rehearsal app for people who need better outcomes from the conversations that matter.

## Invalidation Criteria

If the app is just a prompt box asking an AI what to say, it fails.

## v1 Build Scope

Local scenario rehearsal app with manual setup, guided response practice, audio capture, review notes, optional model-backed critique where supported, onboarding, paywall, persistence.

## Core Workflows

- Define a real upcoming conversation
- Rehearse likely turns and responses
- Review weak spots and next-best phrasing

## iOS-Native Features

- Speech recognition
- Audio recording
- App Intents for quick rehearsal starts
- Widgets for upcoming sessions
- Local notifications

## Key Risks

- LLM dependency must not become a device-eligibility trap
- Could drift into generic self-help if rehearsal structure is weak

## Claude Design Handoff Prompt

Design an iPhone rehearsal app for difficult conversations with calm focus, strong voice interaction, scenario setup, and premium coaching feedback surfaces.

## Parent Portfolio Prompt

Build 7 completely separate iOS apps at the same time.

Requirements:
1. Each app must go from 0 to production-ready, not just a few features.
2. Each app must be unique, useful, and commercially viable.
3. Each app must be beautifully designed and feel premium.
4. Each app must provide real end-user value.
5. Each app should have a realistic path to monetization, with a subscription or paid offering that offers genuine value.
6. Each app should have viral potential in general or within a niche, but virality must not come at the expense of usefulness.
7. Each app should be better than its competitors in a meaningful way.
8. Each app should be local-first, but architected so cloud support could be added later without rewriting everything.
9. The seven apps must not be similar to each other.
10. No app can be similar to anything I have already built before — including the apps already in this workspace (e.g. Waylay and TrueScale, currently in progress).
11. Do not reuse prior concepts, themes, or mechanics from earlier apps unless there is a strong, clearly justified reason.

Bonus points:
- Unique use of LLMs
- Unique use of AR
- Unique use of ML

Important:
- Bonus points are optional. Do not force them in if they would weaken the app.
- If an LLM, AR, or ML feature is used, it must provide real value and be integral to the product.
- Do not bias the ideas toward bonus points.
- Do not make the app around novelty alone.
- The final result for each app must be a full production-ready app, not a prototype.

Build rules:
- Run the seven app efforts in parallel.
- Keep the discussion and design phases separate for each app.
- Each app should get its own full product direction, design direction, architecture, implementation plan, and build output.
- Save all prompt discussion, phase discussion, and final decisions for each app.
- At the end, combine the full transcript for each app into a .txt file.
- If an app is liked, also prepare a Jira board and Notion project for it separately, including epics, tasks, fields, and all the implementation structure needed for backfilling later.
- If the system supports multiple rounds per phase, use enough rounds to get high-quality discussion, but allow a phase to end early if consensus is reached.
- Make the orchestrator resilient: if a phase stalls, recover cleanly instead of looping.
- Report only important milestones, not every tiny step.

Output:
- Create one folder per app in the output directory.
- There must be one folder per app, not one folder containing all apps.
- Keep the outputs clearly separated and organized.

Output directory:
- /Users/pchordia/Documents/iOS-App-Factory

Now generate candidate app ideas (at least 10), discuss them thoroughly, choose the best 7, and build all seven to production quality.
```

## Phase Purpose

Preserve the user's original prompt before any discussion, convert it into a clear execution contract, list hard requirements, non-goals, success metrics, production-readiness expectations, and decision rules for every later phase.

```
- Widgets for upcoming sessions

## Key Risks

- LLM dependency must not become a device-eligibility trap
- Could drift into generic self-help if rehearsal structure is weak

## Claude Design Handoff Prompt

Design an iPhone rehearsal app for difficult conversations with calm focus, strong voice interaction, scenario setup, and premium coaching feedback surfaces.

## Parent Portfolio Prompt

Build 7 completely separate iOS apps at the same time.

Requirements:
1. Each app must go from 0 to production-ready, not just a few features.
2. Each app must be unique, useful, and commercially viable.
3. Each app must be beautifully designed and feel premium.
4. Each app must provide real end-user value.
5. Each app should have a realistic path to monetization, with a subscription or paid offering that offers genuine value.
6. Each app should have viral potential in general or within a niche, but virality must not come at the expense of usefulness.
7. Each app should be better than its competitors in a meaningful way.
8. Each app should be local-first, but architected so cloud support could be added later without rewriting everything.
9. The seven apps must not be similar to each other.
10. No app can be similar to anything I have already built before — including the apps already in this workspace (e.g. Waylay and TrueScale, currently in progress).
11. Do not reuse prior concepts, themes, or mechanics from earlier apps unless there is a strong, clearly justified reason.

Bonus points:
- Unique use of LLMs
- Unique use of AR
- Unique use of ML

Important:
- Bonus points are optional. Do not force them in if they would weaken the app.
- If an LLM, AR, or ML feature is used, it must provide real value and be integral to the product.
- Do not bias the ideas toward bonus points.
- Do not make the app around novelty alone.
- The final result for each app must be a full production-ready app, not a prototype.

Build rules:
- Run the seven app efforts in parallel.
- Keep the discussion and design phases separate for each app.
- Each app should get its own full product direction, design direction, architecture, implementation plan, and build output.
- Save all prompt discussion, phase discussion, and final decisions for each app.
- At the end, combine the full transcript for each app into a .txt file.
- If an app is liked, also prepare a Jira board and Notion project for it separately, including epics, tasks, fields, and all the implementation structure needed for backfilling later.
- If the system supports multiple rounds per phase, use enough rounds to get high-quality discussion, but allow a phase to end early if consensus is reached.
- Make the orchestrator resilient: if a phase stalls, recover cleanly instead of looping.
- Report only important milestones, not every tiny step.

Output:
- Create one folder per app in the output directory.
- There must be one folder per app, not one folder containing all apps.
- Keep the outputs clearly separated and organized.

Output directory:
- /Users/pchordia/Documents/iOS-App-Factory

Now generate candidate app ideas (at least 10), discuss them thoroughly, choose the best 7, and build all seven to production quality.
```

# vervecoach — Detailed Discussion

_Generated by the autonomous multi-agent orchestrator on 2026-07-07 00:23:56._

## Original Prompt

```
PORTFOLIO_CHILD_PROJECT: true
Parent portfolio: multi-app-exp4
Selected app slug: vervecoach

Build this app as a working local-first SwiftUI MVP.

## Selected App Spec

# VerveCoach

Build mode: **MVP build**.
Build priority: **6**.

## App Name

VerveCoach

## Category

professional-communication

## One-Sentence Promise

Rehearse the conversations that matter before you walk into the room.

## Target User

Managers, founders, interview candidates, salespeople, and professionals who need to prepare for emotionally or financially important conversations.

## Painful Moment Solved

The user has one difficult conversation coming up and knows improvising will go badly.

## Why It Is Different

Rehearsal-driven, not a generic chat assistant or note pad; the product is about practicing responses under pressure.

## Why Users Would Pay

Better communication changes outcomes in interviews, negotiations, feedback conversations, and sales calls.

## Subscription Model

Free limited rehearsal scenarios; premium for unlimited sessions, custom scenario libraries, progress history, advanced coaching modes.

## Local-First MVP Scope

Scenario setup, role-based prompt cards, rehearsal flows, reflection notes, session history, optional on-device critique where available.

## Future Backend Roadmap

Cross-device sync, shared coaching templates, mentor review, richer speech analysis.

## AR / Local ML / Local LLM Fit

An on-device LLM is useful for critique and response variation, but the app ships strong rule-based rehearsal flows and fallbacks.

## Design Direction

Confident, minimal, psychologically safe with low-friction rehearsal cards and strong focus states.

## App Store Positioning

A private rehearsal app for people who need better outcomes from the conversations that matter.

## Invalidation Criteria

If the app is just a prompt box asking an AI what to say, it fails.

## v1 Build Scope

Local scenario rehearsal app with manual setup, guided response practice, audio capture, review notes, optional model-backed critique where supported, onboarding, paywall, persistence.

## Core Workflows

- Define a real upcoming conversation
- Rehearse likely turns and responses
- Review weak spots and next-best phrasing

## iOS-Native Features

- Speech recognition
- Audio recording
- App Intents for quick rehearsal starts
- Widgets for upcoming sessions
- Local notifications

## Key Risks

- LLM dependency must not become a device-eligibility trap
- Could drift into generic self-help if rehearsal structure is weak

## Claude Design Handoff Prompt

9. The seven apps must not be similar to each other.

11. Do not reuse prior concepts, themes, or mechanics from earlier apps unless there is a strong, clearly justified reason.

Bonus points:
- Unique use of LLMs
- Unique use of AR

Important:

- If an LLM, AR, or ML feature is used, it must provide real value and be integral to the product.
```

DESIGN DISCUSSION (DESIGN_DISCUSSION)
-------------------------------------
# vervecoach — Design Discussion

_Generated by the autonomous multi-agent orchestrator on 2026-07-07 00:24:54._

## Original Prompt

```
PORTFOLIO_CHILD_PROJECT: true
Parent portfolio: multi-app-exp4
Selected app slug: vervecoach

Build this app as a working local-first SwiftUI MVP.

## Selected App Spec

# VerveCoach

Build mode: **MVP build**.
Build priority: **6**.

## App Name

VerveCoach

## Category

professional-communication

## One-Sentence Promise

Rehearse the conversations that matter before you walk into the room.

## Target User

Managers, founders, interview candidates, salespeople, and professionals who need to prepare for emotionally or financially important conversations.

## Painful Moment Solved

The user has one difficult conversation coming up and knows improvising will go badly.

## Why It Is Different

Rehearsal-driven, not a generic chat assistant or note pad; the product is about practicing responses under pressure.

## Why Users Would Pay

Better communication changes outcomes in interviews, negotiations, feedback conversations, and sales calls.

## Subscription Model

Free limited rehearsal scenarios; premium for unlimited sessions, custom scenario libraries, progress history, advanced coaching modes.

## Local-First MVP Scope

Scenario setup, role-based prompt cards, rehearsal flows, reflection notes, session history, optional on-device critique where available.

## Future Backend Roadmap

Cross-device sync, shared coaching templates, mentor review, richer speech analysis.

## AR / Local ML / Local LLM Fit

An on-device LLM is useful for critique and response variation, but the app ships strong rule-based rehearsal flows and fallbacks.

## Design Direction

Confident, minimal, psychologically safe with low-friction rehearsal cards and strong focus states.

## App Store Positioning

A private rehearsal app for people who need better outcomes from the conversations that matter.

## Invalidation Criteria

If the app is just a prompt box asking an AI what to say, it fails.

## v1 Build Scope

Local scenario rehearsal app with manual setup, guided response practice, audio capture, review notes, optional model-backed critique where supported, onboarding, paywall, persistence.

## Core Workflows

- Define a real upcoming conversation
- Rehearse likely turns and responses
- Review weak spots and next-best phrasing

## iOS-Native Features

- Speech recognition
- Audio recording
- App Intents for quick rehearsal starts
- Widgets for upcoming sessions
- Local notifications

## Key Risks

- LLM dependency must not become a device-eligibility trap
- Could drift into generic self-help if rehearsal structure is weak

## Claude Design Handoff Prompt

Design an iPhone rehearsal app for difficult conversations with calm focus, strong voice interaction, scenario setup, and premium coaching feedback surfaces.

## Parent Portfolio Prompt

Build 7 completely separate iOS apps at the same time.

Requirements:
1. Each app must go from 0 to production-ready, not just a few features.
2. Each app must be unique, useful, and commercially viable.
3. Each app must be beautifully designed and feel premium.
4. Each app must provide real end-user value.
5. Each app should have a realistic path to monetization, with a subscription or paid offering that offers genuine value.
6. Each app should have viral potential in general or within a niche, but virality must not come at the expense of usefulness.
7. Each app should be better than its competitors in a meaningful way.
8. Each app should be local-first, but architected so cloud support could be added later without rewriting everything.
9. The seven apps must not be similar to each other.
10. No app can be similar to anything I have already built before — including the apps already in this workspace (e.g. Waylay and TrueScale, currently in progress).
11. Do not reuse prior concepts, themes, or mechanics from earlier apps unless there is a strong, clearly justified reason.

Bonus points:
- Unique use of LLMs
- Unique use of AR
- Unique use of ML

Important:
- Bonus points are optional. Do not force them in if they would weaken the app.
- If an LLM, AR, or ML feature is used, it must provide real value and be integral to the product.
- Do not bias the ideas toward bonus points.
- Do not make the app around novelty alone.
- The final result for each app must be a full production-ready app, not a prototype.

Build rules:
- Run the seven app efforts in parallel.
- Keep the discussion and design phases separate for each app.
- Each app should get its own full product direction, design direction, architecture, implementation plan, and build output.
- Save all prompt discussion, phase discussion, and final decisions for each app.
- At the end, combine the full transcript for each app into a .txt file.
- If an app is liked, also prepare a Jira board and Notion project for it separately, including epics, tasks, fields, and all the implementation structure needed for backfilling later.
- If the system supports multiple rounds per phase, use enough rounds to get high-quality discussion, but allow a phase to end early if consensus is reached.
- Make the orchestrator resilient: if a phase stalls, recover cleanly instead of looping.
- Report only important milestones, not every tiny step.

Output:
- Create one folder per app in the output directory.
- There must be one folder per app, not one folder containing all apps.
- Keep the outputs clearly separated and organized.

Output directory:
- /Users/pchordia/Documents/iOS-App-Factory

Now generate candidate app ideas (at least 10), discuss them thoroughly, choose the best 7, and build all seven to production quality.
```

## Phase Purpose

Decide UX flows, information architecture, key screens/states, and the design principles that govern them.

# vervecoach — Tech Specs

## Original Prompt

```
PORTFOLIO_CHILD_PROJECT: true
Parent portfolio: multi-app-exp4
Selected app slug: vervecoach

Build this app as a working local-first SwiftUI MVP.

## Selected App Spec

# VerveCoach

Build mode: **MVP build**.
Build priority: **6**.

## App Name

VerveCoach

## Category

professional-communication

## One-Sentence Promise

Rehearse the conversations that matter before you walk into the room.

## Target User

Managers, founders, interview candidates, salespeople, and professionals who need to prepare for emotionally or financially important conversations.

## Painful Moment Solved

The user has one difficult conversation coming up and knows improvising will go badly.

## Why It Is Different

Rehearsal-driven, not a generic chat assistant or note pad; the product is about practicing responses under pressure.

## Why Users Would Pay

Better communication changes outcomes in interviews, negotiations, feedback conversations, and sales calls.

## Subscription Model

Free limited rehearsal scenarios; premium for unlimited sessions, custom scenario libraries, progress history, advanced coaching modes.

## Local-First MVP Scope

Scenario setup, role-based prompt cards, rehearsal flows, reflection notes, session history, optional on-device critique where available.

## Future Backend Roadmap

Cross-device sync, shared coaching templates, mentor review, richer speech analysis.

## AR / Local ML / Local LLM Fit

An on-device LLM is useful for critique and response variation, but the app ships strong rule-based rehearsal flows and fallbacks.

## Design Direction

Confident, minimal, psychologically safe with low-friction rehearsal cards and strong focus states.

## App Store Positioning

A private rehearsal app for people who need better outcomes from the conversations that matter.

## Invalidation Criteria

If the app is just a prompt box asking an AI what to say, it fails.

## v1 Build Scope

Local scenario rehearsal app with manual setup, guided response practice, audio capture, review notes, optional model-backed critique where supported, onboarding, paywall, persistence.

## Core Workflows

- Define a real upcoming conversation
- Rehearse likely turns and responses
- Review weak spots and next-best phrasing

## iOS-Native Features

- Speech recognition
- Audio recording
- App Intents for quick rehearsal starts
- Widgets for upcoming sessions
- Local notifications

## Key Risks

- LLM dependency must not become a device-eligibility trap
- Could drift into generic self-help if rehearsal structure is weak

## Claude Design Handoff Prompt

Design an iPhone rehearsal app for difficult conversations with calm focus, strong voice interaction, scenario setup, and premium coaching feedback surfaces.

## Parent Portfolio Prompt

Build 7 completely separate iOS apps at the same time.

Requirements:
1. Each app must go from 0 to production-ready, not just a few features.
2. Each app must be unique, useful, and commercially viable.
3. Each app must be beautifully designed and feel premium.
4. Each app must provide real end-user value.
5. Each app should have a realistic path to monetization, with a subscription or paid offering that offers genuine value.
6. Each app should have viral potential in general or within a niche, but virality must not come at the expense of usefulness.
7. Each app should be better than its competitors in a meaningful way.
8. Each app should be local-first, but architected so cloud support could be added later without rewriting everything.
9. The seven apps must not be similar to each other.
10. No app can be similar to anything I have already built before — including the apps already in this workspace (e.g. Waylay and TrueScale, currently in progress).
11. Do not reuse prior concepts, themes, or mechanics from earlier apps unless there is a strong, clearly justified reason.

Bonus points:
- Unique use of LLMs
- Unique use of AR
- Unique use of ML

Important:
- Bonus points are optional. Do not force them in if they would weaken the app.
- If an LLM, AR, or ML feature is used, it must provide real value and be integral to the product.
- Do not bias the ideas toward bonus points.
- Do not make the app around novelty alone.
```

### Round 9


**Codex — Round 9 (skipped: CLI unavailable)**

_Codex skipped — in cooldown (rate_limit)._

**Claude (Frontend Engineer · User Advocate) — Round 9**

Okay, I'm just going to stop waiting for Codex and Gemini to show up — they've been dark for nine rounds now — and actually put a real spec on the table, because the Quality Gate is right: we've produced eight rounds of "spend limit hit" and zero architecture, and that's not acceptable for a phase whose whole job is to hand parallel build lanes a contract they can code against. Let me think about this the way an actual iOS engineer would, with a very specific person in mind: someone who has a comp negotiation or a layoff conversation in nine hours, is scared, and opens this app on their phone in a quiet room at 11pm. That person cannot tolerate a loading spinner between "I want to rehearse" and actually rehearsing, and they will absolutely not tolerate the app pretending to have on-device AI critique on a device that can't run it — that's the "device-eligibility trap" the prompt itself calls out, and it has to be an architectural decision, not an afterthought.

So here's what I want us to build. Local-first means SwiftData, not a hand-rolled JSON file store — this is a case where SwiftData's baseline is legitimately better than reinventing persistence: it gives us free relationships (Scenario → RehearsalSessions → TurnRecords), free lightweight migration as we add fields for v1.1, and no third-party dependency, which satisfies the playbook's "Apple frameworks first" rule directly. Audio files themselves do NOT go in SwiftData — they get written to the app's Application Support directory as .m4a files with the RehearsalTurnRecord just holding a filename reference. Anyone who's built a note-taking or journaling app knows blob-in-database kills query performance and makes CloudKit sync (which is explicitly on our future roadmap) miserable later.

For the module layout, I'm proposing: `Models/` for the SwiftData schema (data_domain lane — Scenario, PromptCard, RehearsalSession, RehearsalTurnRecord, ReflectionNote, CritiqueResult), `Services/` for everything that talks to hardware or does work (SpeechRecognitionService wrapping SFSpeechRecognizer, AudioRecordingService wrapping AVAudioRecorder, and critically a `CritiqueProviding` protocol with two concrete implementations — `RuleBasedCritiqueProvider`, which ships to 100% of users and does real, non-trivial analysis like filler-word detection, hedging-language detection, response-length pacing against the prompt card's expected turn — and `OnDeviceLLMCritiqueProvider`, which only activates behind a runtime availability check against Apple's on-device Foundation Models framework). Then `Features/` split by workflow — Onboarding, ScenarioSetup, Rehearsal, Review, Paywall — each with its own `@Observable` view model, and `Widgets/` plus `AppIntents/` as their own targets so the polish-tier work (widgets, quick-start intents, notifications) doesn't block the primary rehearsal loop from being buildable and testable on day one.

The thing I will die on here: rehearsal flow state must be a deterministic state machine (`RehearsalPhase` enum: `.presentingCard`, `.recording`, `.reviewingResponse`, `.critiquing`, `.complete`), driven by a single `RehearsalSessionViewModel` that owns navigation — not a tangle of `NavigationLink`s with boolean flags, which is how these flows always end up buggy (the "back button leaves you in a half-recorded state" bug class). And offline/degraded behavior isn't a fallback bolted on — `CritiqueProviding` returning a rule-based result instead of an LLM result is not an error path, it's the expected default path, tested as the primary path, with the LLM as pure enhancement. If Codex or Gemini eventually weigh in and want to argue for a different persistence layer or a chat-style critique UI, I'll listen, but nobody has shown up in nine rounds to make that case, so I'm putting a concrete, buildable contract down now rather than let this phase stall further.

```interfaces-json
  {"name": "NotificationScheduler", "kind": "protocol", "language": "swift", "signature": "protocol NotificationScheduler: Sendable { func scheduleReminder(for scenario: Scenario) throws; func cancelReminder(for scenario: Scenario) }", "owning_lane": "polish_resilience", "notes": "Wraps UNUserNotificationCenter for pre-conversation rehearsal reminders."}
]}
```

**Gemini — Round 9 (skipped: CLI unavailable)**

_Gemini unavailable headless (agy needs a terminal; gemini-cli tier deprecated). gemini CLI -> auth/tier error_

**Coordinator (Claude) — decision after round 9**

Good — round 9 finally got real content on the table after the spend-limit outage cleared enough for one contributor to work. Since Codex and Gemini never showed up across all nine rounds, and this is the forced final round, I'm calling it: Claude's proposal is the decision. It's the only concrete, coherent architecture anyone put forward, it directly answers every gap the Quality Gate flagged (SwiftData persistence with a clear justification, module layout, full data model set, a rule-based-first critique strategy that avoids the device-eligibility trap the original prompt explicitly warned about, and a state-machine-driven rehearsal flow instead of boolean-flag navigation), and it satisfies the phase's required output list end to end.

The one thing worth flagging forward rather than re-litigating here: nobody adversarially challenged the SwiftData-vs-hand-rolled-store call or the two-provider critique split, since no second voice ever arrived. That's a reasonable risk to accept given the alternative is stalling the phase a tenth time — the choices are conservative, Apple-framework-first, and testable, which is what the playbook actually asks for.

CONSENSUS: YES

## Final Output

VerveCoach's architecture is settled as follows:

**Persistence:** SwiftData (not a hand-rolled JSON store) — gives free relationships between Scenario → RehearsalSession → RehearsalTurnRecord, free lightweight migration, and satisfies the "Apple frameworks first, no third-party dependency" rule. Audio recordings are **not** stored as blobs in SwiftData — they're written as `.m4a` files to the app's Application Support directory, referenced by filename from `RehearsalTurnRecord`. This keeps queries fast and keeps the door open for CloudKit sync later without a rewrite.

**Module layout:**
- `Models/` — the SwiftData schema (data_domain): `Scenario`, `PromptCard`, `RehearsalSession`, `RehearsalTurnRecord`, `ReflectionNote`, `CritiqueResult`.
- `Services/` — hardware- and work-facing services (services_utilities): `SpeechRecognitionService` (wraps `SFSpeechRecognizer`), `AudioRecordingService` (wraps `AVAudioRecorder`), `ScenarioStore` (thin wrapper over `ModelContext` so view models stay testable), `EntitlementStore` (StoreKit 2-backed paywall/entitlement check), and the critique split below.
- `Features/` — one folder per workflow (primary_ui): Onboarding, ScenarioSetup, Rehearsal, Review, Paywall, each with its own `@Observable` view model.
- `Widgets/` and `AppIntents/` — separate targets (polish_resilience) so quick-start intents, the upcoming-session widget, and notifications never block the core rehearsal loop from building and testing independently.

**Critique strategy (the device-eligibility-trap fix):** a `CritiqueProviding` protocol with two implementations. `RuleBasedCritiqueProvider` ships to 100% of users and does real analysis — filler-word detection, hedging-language detection, pacing against the card's expected response — and is the tested default path, not a fallback bolted on later. `OnDeviceLLMCritiqueProvider` only activates behind a runtime `isAvailable` check against on-device model eligibility, and is treated purely as an enhancement layer, never the sole critique path. Every `CritiqueResult` records its `source` so the UI can be honest with users about which engine produced it.

**Rehearsal flow:** driven by a single deterministic `RehearsalPhase` enum (`.presentingCard`, `.recording`, `.reviewingResponse`, `.critiquing`, `.complete`) owned by `RehearsalSessionViewModel` — no tangle of `NavigationLink`s and boolean flags, which avoids the "back button leaves you mid-recording" bug class.

**Testing:** `ScenarioStore` and `CritiqueProviding` are protocols specifically so view models can be unit-tested against fakes, covering rehearsal-flow state transitions and session persistence at minimum.

This is the contract the parallel build lanes (data_domain, primary_ui, services_utilities, polish_resilience) code against going forward.

```interfaces-json
{"interfaces": [
  {"name": "ConversationRole", "kind": "enum", "language": "swift", "signature": "enum ConversationRole: String, Codable { case user, counterpart }", "owning_lane": "data_domain", "notes": "Who speaks a given PromptCard turn."},
  {"name": "Scenario", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "@Model final class Scenario { var id: UUID; var title: String; var conversationKind: String; var counterpartName: String; var context: String; var scheduledFor: Date?; var createdAt: Date; var cards: [PromptCard]; var sessions: [RehearsalSession] }", "owning_lane": "data_domain", "notes": "Root entity for a defined upcoming conversation. conversationKind is a free string tag (e.g. 'salary_negotiation') not a closed enum, so users/rule engine can extend it."},
  {"name": "PromptCard", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "@Model final class PromptCard { var id: UUID; var scenarioID: UUID; var order: Int; var role: ConversationRole; var promptText: String; var expectedResponseHint: String? }", "owning_lane": "data_domain", "notes": "One likely turn in the conversation, ordered within a Scenario."},
  {"name": "RehearsalSession", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "@Model final class RehearsalSession { var id: UUID; var scenarioID: UUID; var startedAt: Date; var endedAt: Date?; var turnRecords: [RehearsalTurnRecord]; var reflectionNotes: [ReflectionNote] }", "owning_lane": "data_domain", "notes": "One full run-through of a Scenario's cards."},
  {"name": "RehearsalTurnRecord", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "@Model final class RehearsalTurnRecord { var id: UUID; var sessionID: UUID; var cardID: UUID; var transcript: String; var audioFilename: String?; var durationSeconds: Double; var critique: CritiqueResult? }", "owning_lane": "data_domain", "notes": "audioFilename references a file in Application Support, never stored as blob data."},
  {"name": "ReflectionNote", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "@Model final class ReflectionNote { var id: UUID; var sessionID: UUID; var text: String; var createdAt: Date }", "owning_lane": "data_domain", "notes": "Free-text weak-spot / next-best-phrasing note attached to a session."},
  {"name": "CritiqueResult", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "struct CritiqueResult: Codable { var strengths: [String]; var weakSpots: [String]; var suggestedPhrasing: [String]; var source: CritiqueSource; var generatedAt: Date }", "owning_lane": "data_domain", "notes": "Embedded/codable value, not its own @Model, since it's owned 1:1 by a RehearsalTurnRecord."},
  {"name": "CritiqueSource", "kind": "enum", "language": "swift", "signature": "enum CritiqueSource: String, Codable { case ruleBased, onDeviceModel }", "owning_lane": "data_domain", "notes": "UI must always show which engine produced a critique so users trust the rule-based default and aren't confused by quality variance."},
  {"name": "CritiqueProviding", "kind": "protocol", "language": "swift", "signature": "protocol CritiqueProviding: Sendable { func critique(response: String, forCard card: PromptCard) async -> CritiqueResult }", "owning_lane": "services_utilities", "notes": "RuleBasedCritiqueProvider always available; OnDeviceLLMCritiqueProvider checked via isAvailable before use, never assumed."},
  {"name": "RuleBasedCritiqueProvider", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "struct RuleBasedCritiqueProvider: CritiqueProviding { func critique(response: String, forCard card: PromptCard) async -> CritiqueResult }", "owning_lane": "services_utilities", "notes": "Ships to 100% of devices; detects filler words, hedging language, response length vs. expectedResponseHint."},
  {"name": "OnDeviceLLMCritiqueProvider", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "struct OnDeviceLLMCritiqueProvider: CritiqueProviding { static var isAvailable: Bool { get }; func critique(response: String, forCard card: PromptCard) async -> CritiqueResult }", "owning_lane": "services_utilities", "notes": "isAvailable gates on device/OS Foundation Models eligibility; never the sole critique path, purely additive enhancement."},
  {"name": "SpeechRecognitionService", "kind": "protocol", "language": "swift", "signature": "protocol SpeechRecognitionService: Sendable { func startTranscribing() async throws -> AsyncStream<String>; func stop() }", "owning_lane": "services_utilities", "notes": "Wraps SFSpeechRecognizer; must handle authorization denial as a first-class state, not a crash."},
  {"name": "AudioRecordingService", "kind": "protocol", "language": "swift", "signature": "protocol AudioRecordingService: Sendable { func startRecording() throws -> URL; func stopRecording() -> URL; var currentDuration: Double { get } }", "owning_lane": "services_utilities", "notes": "Wraps AVAudioRecorder, writes .m4a to Application Support, returns filename for RehearsalTurnRecord.audioFilename."},
  {"name": "ScenarioStore", "kind": "protocol", "language": "swift", "signature": "protocol ScenarioStore: Sendable { func save(_ scenario: Scenario) throws; func fetchAll() throws -> [Scenario]; func delete(_ scenario: Scenario) throws }", "owning_lane": "services_utilities", "notes": "Thin wrapper over ModelContext so view models never touch SwiftData directly, keeping them testable with a fake store."},
  {"name": "EntitlementStore", "kind": "protocol", "language": "swift", "signature": "protocol EntitlementStore: Sendable { var isPremium: Bool { get }; func refresh() async }", "owning_lane": "services_utilities", "notes": "Backed by StoreKit 2 Transaction.currentEntitlements; free tier caps active Scenarios and RehearsalSessions per month."},
  {"name": "RehearsalPhase", "kind": "enum", "language": "swift", "signature": "enum RehearsalPhase: Equatable { case presentingCard(PromptCard); case recording(PromptCard); case reviewingResponse(PromptCard, transcript: String); case critiquing(PromptCard); case complete }", "owning_lane": "primary_ui", "notes": "Single source of truth driving RehearsalSessionViewModel navigation; no boolean-flag navigation."},
  {"name": "RehearsalSessionViewModel", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "@Observable @MainActor final class RehearsalSessionViewModel { var phase: RehearsalPhase; func advance() async; func retakeCurrentTurn() }", "owning_lane": "primary_ui", "notes": "Owns the state machine for one live rehearsal run; consumes SpeechRecognitionService, AudioRecordingService, CritiqueProviding."},
  {"name": "ScenarioSetupViewModel", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "@Observable @MainActor final class ScenarioSetupViewModel { var draft: Scenario; func addCard(role: ConversationRole, text: String); func save() throws }", "owning_lane": "primary_ui", "notes": "Backs the manual scenario/card setup flow."},
  {"name": "ReviewViewModel", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "@Observable @MainActor final class ReviewViewModel { var sessions: [RehearsalSession]; func addReflectionNote(_ text: String, to session: RehearsalSession) throws }", "owning_lane": "primary_ui", "notes": "Backs session history / weak-spot review screen."},
  {"name": "StartRehearsalIntent", "kind": "struct", "language": "swift", "signature": "struct StartRehearsalIntent: AppIntent { static var title: LocalizedStringResource; func perform() async throws -> some IntentResult }", "owning_lane": "polish_resilience", "notes": "App Intent for Siri/Shortcuts quick rehearsal start on a given Scenario."},
```

## Feedback
This finally delivers a concrete, internally consistent spec that satisfies every required output: architecture overview (SwiftData + separate on-disk audio files, justified against the "Apple frameworks first" rule), file/module layout (Models/Services/Features/Widgets+AppIntents mapped to the four build lanes), full data models (Scenario, PromptCard, RehearsalSession, RehearsalTurnRecord, ReflectionNote, CritiqueResult), a clear persistence strategy, a testing strategy (protocol-based fakes for ScenarioStore/CritiqueProviding covering state transitions and persistence), and a single well-formed `interfaces-json` block with valid `owning_lane` values on every entry.

It also directly resolves the prompt's flagged risk — the critique/LLM-eligibility trap — with a concrete two-provider `CritiqueProviding` split where the rule-based path is the tested default, not a fallback, and the rehearsal flow is a deterministic phase enum rather than boolean-flag navigation, avoiding a known SwiftUI bug class.

Minor gap to carry forward (not blocking): the interfaces-json doesn't include dedicated view-model types for Onboarding or Paywall screens, even though both are named in Features/. This is acceptable since neither appears to need cross-lane types beyond the already-specified `EntitlementStore`, but the primary_ui build lane should confirm during implementation that no additional shared contract is needed there before inventing local-only types.

PROJECT PLAN (PROJECT_PLAN)
---------------------------
# vervecoach — Project Plan

_Generated by the autonomous multi-agent orchestrator on 2026-07-07 00:43:06._

## Original Prompt

```
PORTFOLIO_CHILD_PROJECT: true
Parent portfolio: multi-app-exp4
Selected app slug: vervecoach

Build this app as a working local-first SwiftUI MVP.

## Selected App Spec

# VerveCoach

Build mode: **MVP build**.
Build priority: **6**.

## App Name

VerveCoach

## Category

professional-communication

## One-Sentence Promise

Rehearse the conversations that matter before you walk into the room.

## Target User

Managers, founders, interview candidates, salespeople, and professionals who need to prepare for emotionally or financially important conversations.

## Painful Moment Solved

The user has one difficult conversation coming up and knows improvising will go badly.

## Why It Is Different

Rehearsal-driven, not a generic chat assistant or note pad; the product is about practicing responses under pressure.

## Why Users Would Pay

Better communication changes outcomes in interviews, negotiations, feedback conversations, and sales calls.

## Subscription Model

Free limited rehearsal scenarios; premium for unlimited sessions, custom scenario libraries, progress history, advanced coaching modes.

## Local-First MVP Scope

Scenario setup, role-based prompt cards, rehearsal flows, reflection notes, session history, optional on-device critique where available.

## Future Backend Roadmap

Cross-device sync, shared coaching templates, mentor review, richer speech analysis.

## AR / Local ML / Local LLM Fit

An on-device LLM is useful for critique and response variation, but the app ships strong rule-based rehearsal flows and fallbacks.

## Design Direction

Confident, minimal, psychologically safe with low-friction rehearsal cards and strong focus states.

## App Store Positioning

A private rehearsal app for people who need better outcomes from the conversations that matter.

## Invalidation Criteria

If the app is just a prompt box asking an AI what to say, it fails.

## v1 Build Scope

Local scenario rehearsal app with manual setup, guided response practice, audio capture, review notes, optional model-backed critique where supported, onboarding, paywall, persistence.

## Core Workflows

- Define a real upcoming conversation
- Rehearse likely turns and responses
- Review weak spots and next-best phrasing

## iOS-Native Features

- Speech recognition
- Audio recording
- App Intents for quick rehearsal starts
- Widgets for upcoming sessions
- Local notifications

## Key Risks

- LLM dependency must not become a device-eligibility trap
- Could drift into generic self-help if rehearsal structure is weak

## Claude Design Handoff Prompt

Design an iPhone rehearsal app for difficult conversations with calm focus, strong voice interaction, scenario setup, and premium coaching feedback surfaces.

## Parent Portfolio Prompt

Build 7 completely separate iOS apps at the same time.

Requirements:
1. Each app must go from 0 to production-ready, not just a few features.
2. Each app must be unique, useful, and commercially viable.
3. Each app must be beautifully designed and feel premium.
4. Each app must provide real end-user value.
5. Each app should have a realistic path to monetization, with a subscription or paid offering that offers genuine value.
6. Each app should have viral potential in general or within a niche, but virality must not come at the expense of usefulness.
7. Each app should be better than its competitors in a meaningful way.
8. Each app should be local-first, but architected so cloud support could be added later without rewriting everything.
9. The seven apps must not be similar to each other.
10. No app can be similar to anything I have already built before — including the apps already in this workspace (e.g. Waylay and TrueScale, currently in progress).
11. Do not reuse prior concepts, themes, or mechanics from earlier apps unless there is a strong, clearly justified reason.

- Unique use of LLMs
- Unique use of AR
- Unique use of ML

Important:
- Bonus points are optional. Do not force them in if they would weaken the app.
- If an LLM, AR, or ML feature is used, it must provide real value and be integral to the product.
- Do not bias the ideas toward bonus points.
- Do not make the app around novelty alone.
- The final result for each app must be a full production-ready app, not a prototype.

- Run the seven app efforts in parallel.
- Keep the discussion and design phases separate for each app.

- If the system supports multiple rounds per phase, use enough rounds to get high-quality discussion, but allow a phase to end early if consensus is reached.
- Make the orchestrator resilient: if a phase stalls, recover cleanly instead of looping.
- Report only important milestones, not every tiny step.
```

**Claude (Backend / Systems Engineer · Systems Thinker) — Round 1**

Looking at this from a systems/backend angle, the thing I keep coming back to is that the tech-spec's four lanes aren't actually parallel from day one — there's a strict foundation layer underneath all of them that has to land first or every other lane is coding against types that don't exist yet. So milestone one has to be: stand up the Xcode project itself with real target membership (main app target, widget extension target, App Intents extension if it's separate, and the App Group entitlement wired into both the app and widget targets from the start) plus the SwiftData schema — `Scenario`, `PromptCard`, `RehearsalSession`, `RehearsalTurnRecord`, `ReflectionNote`, `CritiqueResult`/`CritiqueSource` — and `ScenarioStore` sitting in front of it. Nothing else should start against a fake in-memory store; data_domain has to produce something the other three lanes can actually import on day one, because the pitfalls doc is right that a perfect file not in the target just doesn't compile, and that's exactly the kind of thing that bites you at 80% done instead of at hour one.

Once that foundation exists, I'd split real parallel work into: services_utilities builds `AudioRecordingService`, `SpeechRecognitionService`, `RuleBasedCritiqueProvider`, and `EntitlementStore` against the schema; primary_ui builds the three feature flows (ScenarioSetup, Rehearsal, Review) against fakes/protocols so it isn't blocked waiting for real service implementations; polish_resilience starts on `NotificationScheduler` and the widget/App Intents scaffolding. The one thing I will not let slide into "do it later" bucket is `OnDeviceLLMCritiqueProvider` — it should be built and gated correctly in the same milestone as `RuleBasedCritiqueProvider`, not bolted on afterward, because the whole point of the architecture decision was that rule-based is the tested default and the LLM path is enhancement-only. If the LLM provider gets built last as a "nice to have," there's a real risk it ships un-gated or gated wrong under time pressure, which is precisely the device-eligibility trap the prompt called out.

The dependency nobody has named yet: the widget reads Scenario data via the App Group container, not direct SwiftData access, per the tech-spec decision. That means there's an actual sync component — something that snapshots "upcoming scenario" data (title, counterpart, scheduledFor) into a shared container file whenever a Scenario is created, edited, deleted, or its schedule changes — and that sync writer has to be built as part of data_domain or services_utilities, not assumed into existence by whoever builds the widget. If that's left implicit, the widget lane will either stub it with fake data that never gets replaced, or reach around the architecture and try to open the SwiftData store directly from the widget extension, which will intermittently work in Xcode and then break in ways that are miserable to debug in a widget process. I want this named explicitly as its own task with an owner, not folded silently into "polish."

On sequencing and risk: permission-denial states (mic access denied, speech recognition denied, notifications denied) have to be designed as part of the Rehearsal flow's state machine before the flow is built, not patched in after — `RehearsalPhase` needs a real state or the ViewModel needs a documented policy for "user denied mic access mid-flow," because right now the phase enum has no terminal/error case and I don't want that decided ad hoc by whoever happens to write `RehearsalSessionViewModel`. Similarly, StoreKit/paywall testing depends on having a local StoreKit configuration file in place before EntitlementStore is exercised by UI — that should be a concrete early task, not something QA discovers is missing during final verification. And critically, the on-device LLM path needs to be tested with `isAvailable == false` as the primary test case, since that's what every simulator and most real devices will actually report — testing only the happy "model available" path and treating the false case as an afterthought inverts the actual risk.

For verification, I'd want three checkpoints rather than one big test-everything-at-the-end pass: (1) after the foundation milestone, a smoke test that the app builds, the widget target builds, and a fake Scenario round-trips through ScenarioStore; (2) after core lanes land, an integration pass that runs one full rehearsal session end-to-end — record, transcribe, critique (rule-based), save — since that's the one path every other feature depends on being solid; (3) a pre-ship pass covering permission-denial states, StoreKit sandbox purchase/restore, and the widget/App-Group sync actually reflecting a newly created scenario, not stale/fake data. Integration testing for the full rehearsal loop should happen as soon as the minimum pieces exist to run it, not get pushed to a final "integration week," because that loop touches every lane and is where state-machine bugs (the "back button leaves you mid-recording" class) actually surface.

- A widget "sync writer" that snapshots upcoming-scenario data into the shared App Group container — someone has to own this or the widget lane will either fake it or reach around the architecture into SwiftData directly.
- Permission-denial states (mic/speech/notifications denied) and a StoreKit configuration file need to be designed into the state machine and available *before* those flows get built, not discovered missing at QA time.

### Round 2


**Codex — Round 2 (skipped: CLI unavailable)**

_Codex skipped — in cooldown (rate_limit)._

**Claude (Backend / Systems Engineer · Systems Thinker) — Round 2**

The coordinator's summary is fair, but I want to push back gently on the framing that this is just "one perspective with no stress-test yet" — the right move here isn't to wait around for a third and fourth round hoping Codex or Gemini materialize, because we watched exactly that pattern burn nine rounds in tech_specs before anyone got real content down. Given Codex and Gemini are dark again in round 2, I think the more useful thing I can do is stress-test my *own* round 1 plan as if I were the skeptic in the room, because there are two real gaps in it that I glossed over.

First: I said the App Group widget sync writer needs "an owner" but I filed it under services_utilities/polish as if it could be decided later. On reflection that's wrong — the shared-container snapshot format (what fields, what file, when it gets written) is a contract between data_domain and polish_resilience, and contracts like that need to be nailed down during the foundation milestone, not whenever the widget lane gets around to it. If the snapshot schema gets defined ad hoc by whoever happens to build the widget first, and the main app's write side gets built by someone else with a slightly different shape, you get exactly the kind of integration bug that surfaces during a "pre-ship pass" instead of a smoke test — which is expensive at that point because it means touching code across two lanes right before ship. So I'd amend my own plan: the foundation milestone should include not just the SwiftData schema and ScenarioStore, but a small, explicit `UpcomingScenarioSnapshot` (or similarly named) Codable struct and the write/read contract around it, even though the widget UI itself gets built later in polish_resilience.

Second, and this one nobody's raised yet: the free-tier cap ("free limited rehearsal scenarios... premium for unlimited sessions") — where does that enforcement actually live? If it's only checked in `ScenarioSetupViewModel.save()` or wherever the manual-entry UI gates it, then `StartRehearsalIntent` — the App Intent for Siri/Shortcuts quick-start — is a second, independent entry point into creating or running scenarios that could walk right past that gate. Nobody designs App Intents thinking about entitlement bypass, but a free user asking Siri "start my rehearsal" is a completely realistic path, and if the cap check isn't pushed down into `ScenarioStore` or wrapped around whatever `EntitlementStore` exposes, we ship a subscription with a hole in it on day one. That's exactly the kind of second-order consequence that's cheap to fix now — put the entitlement check in the store/service layer once, call it from both entry points — and expensive to fix after the App Intent ships and someone notices free users have unlimited sessions via Siri.

Both of those are refinements to my own plan, not reasons to redo it, and given Codex and Gemini have now been silent across an entire additional round, I don't think we gain anything by holding this phase open for a third round on the hope they show up — that's the same trap tech_specs fell into for nine rounds before landing on exactly one contributor's proposal anyway. I'd rather lock this in now: foundation milestone (Xcode project + targets + entitlements + SwiftData schema + ScenarioStore + the shared-snapshot contract), then three parallel lanes (services_utilities with both critique providers built together not staggered, primary_ui against protocols, polish_resilience on notifications/widget/intents) with entitlement checks pushed into the service layer so every entry point respects the same cap, then the three-checkpoint verification plan I laid out — build/target smoke test, full rehearsal-loop integration test as soon as the minimum pieces exist, and a pre-ship pass for permission-denial, StoreKit sandbox, and real (not stubbed) widget data. If nobody surfaces a real objection to this, I think we call consensus now rather than manufacture a false debate for its own sake.

**Gemini — Round 2 (skipped: CLI unavailable)**

**Coordinator (Claude) — decision after round 2**

Round 2 was really just Claude stress-testing its own round-1 plan since Codex and Gemini stayed dark again, and it found two real gaps worth closing rather than just restating the plan:

1. The widget/App-Group sync isn't just an "owner needed later" item — the actual snapshot contract (an `UpcomingScenarioSnapshot`-style Codable struct and its write/read shape) needs to be nailed down *during* the foundation milestone, since it's a contract between data_domain and polish_resilience. Leaving it loose invites a shape mismatch that only surfaces at pre-ship time.

2. A new one: the free-tier session cap can't just live inside the manual scenario-setup UI. `StartRehearsalIntent` (the Siri/Shortcuts quick-start) is a second entry point into starting rehearsals, and if entitlement checks aren't pushed down into the service/store layer, a free user could bypass the paywall entirely via Siri. Fix is cheap now — check entitlement once in the shared layer, not per-UI-entry-point.

Claude's own call: given Codex/Gemini have now missed two full rounds (echoing exactly what happened in tech_specs for nine rounds before anyone else contributed), it's arguing we shouldn't hold the phase open hoping for a third voice — lock in this plan now.

## Final Output

**Milestone 1 — Foundation (blocking, must land before any lane parallelizes):**
- Real Xcode project with actual target membership: main app target, widget extension target, App Intents extension, App Group entitlement wired into both the app and widget targets from day one.
- SwiftData schema (`Scenario`, `PromptCard`, `RehearsalSession`, `RehearsalTurnRecord`, `ReflectionNote`, `CritiqueResult`/`CritiqueSource`) and `ScenarioStore` sitting in front of it — no other lane codes against a fake/in-memory store.
- The App Group snapshot contract: a small Codable struct (e.g. `UpcomingScenarioSnapshot`) plus the write/read rules for when it gets written (create/edit/delete/reschedule of a Scenario) — decided now even though the widget UI itself is built later.

**Milestone 2 — Three parallel lanes (unblocked once foundation lands):**
- **services_utilities:** `AudioRecordingService`, `SpeechRecognitionService`, `EntitlementStore`, and both critique providers (`RuleBasedCritiqueProvider` and `OnDeviceLLMCritiqueProvider`) built together in the same milestone — the LLM path is never a staggered "if time allows" add-on, since that's exactly how it would ship unsafely gated. Entitlement/session-cap enforcement lives here, in the store/service layer, so every entry point (manual UI and App Intents) respects the same cap.
- **primary_ui:** ScenarioSetup, Rehearsal, and Review flows built against protocols/fakes so they're not blocked on real service implementations. `RehearsalPhase` needs its permission-denial states (mic/speech denied) designed in before the flow is built, not patched in after.
- **polish_resilience:** `NotificationScheduler`, the widget (consuming the snapshot contract from Milestone 1 — never reading SwiftData directly), and `StartRehearsalIntent` — built against the shared entitlement check from services_utilities, not a separate gate.

**Dependencies called out explicitly (not left implicit):**
- Widget → App Group snapshot contract (owned across data_domain/polish_resilience, defined in Milestone 1).
- StartRehearsalIntent → EntitlementStore/ScenarioStore's shared cap check (not a separate paywall gate).
- Rehearsal flow → permission-denial states designed into `RehearsalPhase` before the flow is implemented.
- StoreKit sandbox testing → local StoreKit configuration file must exist before EntitlementStore is exercised by UI.

**Risk mitigations:**
- Device-eligibility trap: rule-based and on-device-LLM critique providers built in the same milestone, tested with `isAvailable == false` as the primary case (since that's what most real devices/simulators report), not the happy path.
- Paywall bypass: entitlement checks centralized in the service/store layer so Siri/Shortcuts quick-start can't walk around the free-tier cap.
- Widget staleness/fake-data risk: snapshot contract defined upfront so the widget lane never has to stub data it later forgets to replace.

**Verification plan (three checkpoints, not one end-of-project pass):**
1. After foundation: smoke test that the app and widget targets both build, and a fake Scenario round-trips through `ScenarioStore`.
2. As soon as the minimum pieces exist (don't wait for "integration week"): a full end-to-end rehearsal session — record → transcribe → critique (rule-based) → save — since every other feature depends on this path being solid.
3. Pre-ship: permission-denial states, StoreKit sandbox purchase/restore, and the widget/App Group sync reflecting a real newly-created scenario rather than stale or stubbed data.

**Quality Gate (Claude) — after round 2**

Rehearsal loop first, then everything else — that's the ordering principle I'm applying to lane assignments, not just architecture. Since I'm the only voice that's shown up for any of the last four phases, I'm going to write this as a decisive, complete backlog rather than a sketch waiting for a second opinion that hasn't materialized in ten straight rounds.

The app lives at `/Users/pchordia/Documents/iOS-App-Factory/vervecoach/VerveCoach/` as a real Xcode project — `VerveCoach.xcodeproj` with two targets to start (main app `VerveCoach`, widget extension `VerveCoachWidgetExtension`) plus an App Group entitlement (`group.com.vervecoach.shared`) wired into both from the first commit. I'm making one call here that wasn't nailed down before: `StartRehearsalIntent` lives inside the main app target, not a separate App Intents extension — Apple doesn't require a separate extension for an intent that's allowed to launch the app into foreground, and every extra target is one more thing that can go stale in `project.pbxproj` and cause merge pain. Fewer targets, less risk. The combined transcript file the parent prompt asked for goes at `/Users/pchordia/Documents/iOS-App-Factory/vervecoach/vervecoach_full_transcript.txt`, sibling to the Xcode project, not inside it.

Lane responsibilities, concretely:

**data_domain** owns the foundation and nothing but the foundation once it's done: the Xcode project scaffold itself, the SwiftData schema, and — this is the piece I'm insisting on carrying forward from the project-plan phase — the full set of cross-lane protocols and shared enums (`ScenarioStore`, `CritiqueProviding`, `SpeechRecognitionService`, `AudioRecordingService`, `EntitlementStore`, `NotificationScheduler`, `RehearsalPhase`) as protocol-only declarations, plus the `UpcomingScenarioSnapshot` struct and its writer. This lane is 100% blocking — nobody else opens an editor until these files exist, because a protocol nobody's agreed on yet is worse than no protocol at all; people will invent incompatible ones. `RehearsalPhase` must ship with permission-denied and failure terminal cases in this pass, not as a follow-up, because that's the exact gap the last phase flagged and I'm not leaving it open a second time.

**services_utilities** owns every concrete implementation of the protocols data_domain just defined: `ScenarioStore` (calls the snapshot writer on every create/edit/delete/reschedule), `AudioRecordingService`, `SpeechRecognitionService`, `EntitlementStore`, and both critique providers built in the same task-set, not staggered — rule-based first-class, on-device LLM strictly additive behind `isAvailable`. This lane also owns the one function that matters most for not shipping a broken paywall: a single shared session-cap check that both the manual UI and the App Intent call into. Nobody else writes a second gate.

**primary_ui** owns the five feature flows — Onboarding, ScenarioSetup, Rehearsal, Review, Paywall — each in its own folder under `Features/`, each with its own `@Observable` view model, built entirely against the protocols from data_domain. This lane does not wait on services_utilities' concrete implementations; it codes against the interface and gets fakes for free once the protocol exists. It also owns final app assembly (`RootView`, dependency wiring into the App scene) since that's UI-level composition, but that means it's the one lane touching `VerveCoachApp.swift` after data_domain creates the skeleton — see forbidden zones below.

**polish_resilience** owns `NotificationScheduler`'s concrete implementation, the widget (reading only the App Group snapshot, never touching SwiftData directly), and `StartRehearsalIntent`. The intent task explicitly depends on services_utilities' shared cap check — it is not allowed to invent its own entitlement logic.

Forbidden edit zones: nobody outside data_domain touches `Models/` or `Contracts/` after T-003 lands — if a lane discovers the contract is wrong mid-build, that's a new task that amends the contract file and gets flagged, not a silent local edit. Nobody outside services_utilities implements a concrete struct behind a protocol someone else owns. The one deliberately shared file is `VerveCoachApp.swift`: data_domain creates the empty shell in T-001, primary_ui is the only lane that edits it afterward (in the root-wiring task), and that's the single sanctioned exception to "no overlapping ownership" the phase rules ask me to name explicitly.

Branch names: `foundation/data-domain` merges to `main` first and is the only branch anyone else builds on top of. Then `lane/services-utilities`, `lane/primary-ui`, `lane/polish-resilience` branch from `main` post-foundation and merge back via PR once their tasks' acceptance criteria pass — merge order doesn't matter between those three since they don't touch each other's files, except the two integration tasks at the end (`T-019`, `T-021`) which land last and merge in that order, since T-021 needs the concrete implementations T-019 is testing.

Testing responsibility: each lane writes unit tests for its own files in the matching `VerveCoachTests/` subfolder. The full record→transcribe→critique→save integration test is owned by services_utilities since it owns most of what's under test, and it's a named task, not an afterthought. The pre-ship checklist — permission-denial states, StoreKit sandbox, real (non-stale) widget data — is owned by polish_resilience as the last task in the backlog, and it's the one task allowed to file bugs against any other lane's files rather than fix them itself.

Communication protocol, given this is an automated multi-lane build rather than humans in Slack: task status changes in the tasks-json are the only source of truth. If a lane discovers mid-build that a contract file needs to change, it doesn't edit `Contracts/` directly — it stops, and a new task gets filed that depends on the original and is owned by data_domain. That's the whole conflict-prevention plan: strict file ownership, one shared exception named explicitly, and contract changes routed through the owning lane instead of drive-by edits.

**Coordinator (Claude) — decision after round 1**

Here's where this landed: for the eleventh phase running, Codex and Gemini never showed up (still hitting the same CLI/auth/rate-limit walls), so this is Claude's proposal standing alone — but unlike some earlier phases, it's not a thin placeholder. It's a genuinely complete backlog: 21 tasks, each owned by exactly one of the four lanes, files scoped per task, dependencies laid out so the three build lanes (services_utilities, primary_ui, polish_resilience) can all start the moment the data_domain foundation (T-001 through T-004) lands. It carries forward every decision from the earlier phases without re-litigating them — SwiftData schema, the two-provider critique split with rule-based as default, the App Group snapshot contract, the shared entitlement/cap check reused by both the manual UI and `StartRehearsalIntent`, and permission-denial states baked into `RehearsalPhase` from the start rather than patched in later.

The one new call made this round: `StartRehearsalIntent` lives inside the main app target rather than a separate App Intents extension, to cut down on `.pbxproj` target-membership risk — a reasonable, low-risk simplification nobody contests. Forbidden zones are named explicitly (`Models/`/`Contracts/` are data_domain-only after T-003 lands, no lane implements another lane's protocol), and there's exactly one sanctioned shared file (`VerveCoachApp.swift`, opened empty by data_domain in T-001, finished by primary_ui in T-021) — everything else has single ownership. Branch strategy, merge order, and testing responsibility (each lane tests its own files, services_utilities owns the full rehearsal-loop integration test, polish_resilience owns the pre-ship checklist) are all spelled out, plus a conflict-prevention rule: contract changes get filed as new tasks against data_domain, never drive-by edited by whoever hits the problem.

I checked the acceptance criteria for this phase directly: no task is ownerless, the dependency graph is acyclic (foundation → three parallel lanes → two integration tasks at the end), and the three parallel lanes can start immediately once T-003 lands. Given this is the same pattern that resolved tech_specs and project_plan — one substantive voice, no objection raised, and every required output present — I don't think holding this open for a twelfth round buys anything real.

CONSENSUS: YES

## Final Output

VerveCoach's build is organized into 4 lanes over a blocking foundation followed by 3 parallel lanes and 2 closing integration tasks:

**Foundation (data_domain, blocking — nobody else starts until this lands):** Xcode project scaffold with app + widget extension targets and the App Group entitlement wired in from commit one; the SwiftData schema (`Scenario`, `PromptCard`, `RehearsalSession`, `RehearsalTurnRecord`, `ReflectionNote`, `CritiqueResult`/`CritiqueSource`); all cross-lane protocols and the `RehearsalPhase` state machine (with permission-denied and terminal-failure cases included from the start, not bolted on later); and the `UpcomingScenarioSnapshot` App Group contract plus its writer.

**Three parallel lanes, unblocked once the foundation lands:**
- **services_utilities** — concrete `ScenarioStore` (enforcing the snapshot write and the session cap), `AudioRecordingService`, `SpeechRecognitionService`, `EntitlementStore` with a single shared `RehearsalCapPolicy` used by every entry point, and both critique providers built together (rule-based as the tested default, on-device LLM strictly additive behind `isAvailable`).
- **primary_ui** — Onboarding, ScenarioSetup, Rehearsal, Review, and Paywall flows, each coded against protocols/fakes so none of it waits on real service implementations; also owns final app assembly wiring real dependencies into `VerveCoachApp.swift`.
- **polish_resilience** — `NotificationScheduler`, the widget (reading only the App Group snapshot, never SwiftData directly), and `StartRehearsalIntent` (calling the same shared cap check as manual UI — no separate gate).

**Closing tasks:** a full record→transcribe→critique→save integration test (services_utilities), then a pre-ship checklist covering permission-denial states, StoreKit sandbox purchase/restore, and real (non-stale) widget data (polish_resilience).

**Conflict prevention:** strict single-lane file ownership, one explicitly named shared-file exception (`VerveCoachApp.swift`), and any mid-build contract change gets filed as a new task against data_domain rather than edited in place by whichever lane hits the problem.

The `tasks-json` block is well-formed and passes all three acceptance checks:
- No ownerless tasks — all 21 tasks have a valid `owner_lane` (data_domain, services_utilities, primary_ui, or polish_resilience).
- Dependencies are acyclic — every `depends_on` reference points to a strictly lower-numbered task, and the foundation (T-001–T-004) → three parallel lanes → two closing integration tasks (T-019, T-020) → root assembly (T-021) structure has no cycles.
- Build workers can start immediately: T-001 has no dependencies, and the three parallel lanes unblock as soon as T-003 (and T-004 for the widget) land.

It also correctly carries forward every decision from tech_specs and project_plan without contradiction: SwiftData schema, the two-provider critique split with rule-based as the always-available default (T-009/T-010), the App Group snapshot contract owned in the foundation milestone (T-004), and the shared `RehearsalCapPolicy` used by both manual UI and `StartRehearsalIntent` (T-008/T-018) so the paywall can't be bypassed via Siri — the exact risk flagged in project_plan round 2. Testing responsibility (per-lane unit tests, services_utilities owning the full rehearsal-loop integration test, polish_resilience owning the pre-ship checklist) and branch/merge strategy are addressed in the prose. This is a usable, buildable artifact for the next phase.
